# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

\"pkg/services/dashboards/accesscontrol.go\", \"symbol\": \"GetInheritedScopes\"}\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"The Grafana user permission model is implemented across multiple files in the grafana/grafana repository, defining a three-tier role system (Viewer/Editor/Admin) with role-to-permission mapping, permission guards via middleware, and folder/dashboard permission inheritance.\\n\\n**Three-Tier Role Definition:**\\nThe core role types are defined in `pkg/apimachinery/identity/role_type.go`, which defines RoleType as a string enum with four values: RoleNone (10), RoleViewer (20), RoleEditor (30), and RoleAdmin (40). The precedence map shows the role hierarchy, with Admin being highest privilege. The `Includes()` method checks if one role includes another based on this precedence. These roles are also defined in `pkg/services/org/model.go` as organizational roles.\\n\\n**Role-to-Permission Mapping:**\\nThe basic role definitions are built in `pkg/services/accesscontrol/roles.go` using the `BuildBasicRoleDefinitions()` function, which creates RoleDTO objects for Admin, Editor, Viewer, and None roles with initial empty permissions. The `DeclareFixedRoles()` function registers fixed roles for various resources like LDAP, Org Users, Settings, and Stats, each mapped to built-in roles via the RoleRegistration struct. Dashboard-specific roles are registered in `pkg/services/accesscontrol/ossaccesscontrol/dashboard.go` with three roles (Viewer/Editor/Admin) having corresponding permissions: DashboardViewActions, DashboardEditActions, and DashboardAdminActions. Folder-specific roles are registered in `pkg/services/accesscontrol/ossaccesscontrol/folder.go` with similar three-tier structure: FolderViewActions (includes folders:read, dashboards:read, alerts:read, etc.), FolderEditActions (includes write/delete), and FolderAdminActions (includes permissions management).\\n\\n**Models and Data Structures:**\\n`pkg/services/accesscontrol/models.go` defines core structures: RoleDTO (contains role name, display name, description, and permissions array), Permission (action and scope fields), and ResourcePermission (user/team/role associations with actions and scope). `pkg/services/dashboards/dashboardaccess/dashboard_access.go` defines PermissionType enum with three values: PERMISSION_VIEW (1), PERMISSION_EDIT (2), and PERMISSION_ADMIN (4). `pkg/services/dashboards/models.go` defines DashboardACL and DashboardACLInfoDTO structures for storing dashboard-level permissions associated with users, teams, or roles.\\n\\n**Permission Guard Middleware:**\\nThe permission enforcement happens through middleware in `pkg/services/accesscontrol/middleware.go`. The `Middleware()` function returns a handler that uses the `authorize()` function to check permissions. The authorize function calls the AccessControl's `Evaluate()` method (defined in `pkg/services/accesscontrol/accesscontrol.go` interface) with an Evaluator. The `Evaluator` interface (in `pkg/services/accesscontrol/evaluator.go`) uses `EvalPermission()` to check if a user has required actions and scopes. Permission evaluation is ultimately performed by the `Checker()` function in `pkg/services/accesscontrol/checker.go`, which compares user permissions against required evaluator conditions.\\n\\n**AccessControl Service Implementation:**\\nThe Service interface (in `pkg/services/accesscontrol/accesscontrol.go`) defines key methods: `Evaluate()` for permission checks, `DeclareFixedRoles()` for role registration, `GetUserPermissions()` for retrieving user permissions, and `GetRoleByName()` for role lookup. The implementation is in `pkg/services/accesscontrol/acimpl/service.go`, which loads basic role definitions, manages permission caches, and coordinates with the Store interface for permission queries. The Service maintains a roles map and uses a database store to retrieve user permissions based on built-in roles, team memberships, and explicit user role assignments.\\n\\n**Folder and Dashboard Permission Inheritance:**\\nDashboard and folder permissions support hierarchical inheritance through `pkg/services/dashboards/accesscontrol.go`. The `GetInheritedScopes()` function retrieves all parent folder UIDs for a given folder, enabling permission inheritance up the folder tree. Dashboards inherit permissions from their parent folder. The `NewDashboardUIDScopeResolver()` and `NewFolderUIDScopeResolver()` functions resolve dashboard/folder scopes to include both the resource's own scope and all ancestor folder scopes. When a dashboard is in a folder, the permission check includes: the dashboard's own scope (dashboards:uid:{uid}), the folder's scope (folders:uid:{uid}), and all ancestor folder scopes recursively. Dashboard permissions are managed through `ProvideDashboardPermissions()` in `pkg/services/accesscontrol/ossaccesscontrol/dashboard.go`, which sets up the InheritedScopesSolver to call GetInheritedScopes(). Folder permissions are managed through `ProvideFolderPermissions()` in `pkg/services/accesscontrol/ossaccesscontrol/folder.go` with similar inheritance support. The PermissionsService interface (in `pkg/services/accesscontrol/accesscontrol.go`) defines methods for managing resource permissions: `GetPermissions()`, `SetUserPermission()`, `SetTeamPermission()`, `SetBuiltInRolePermission()`, all supporting the View/Edit/Admin permission levels for folders and dashboards.\\n\\n**API Endpoints:**\\nDashboard permissions are exposed via REST APIs in `pkg/api/dashboard_permission.go` with endpoints for getting, updating, and managing dashboard ACLs. Folder permissions are exposed in `pkg/api/folder_permission.go` with similar endpoints. Both use the DashboardPermissionsService and FolderPermissionsService (aliases for PermissionsService) to manage permissions. Route registration in `pkg/api/folder.go` and `pkg/api/dashboard.go` uses the `authorize()` middleware with evaluators checking for specific actions like ActionFoldersRead, ActionFoldersWrite, ActionDashboardsRead, etc.\\n\\n**Summary:**\\nThe implementation creates a complete three-tier RBAC system where: (1) Role types (Viewer/Editor/Admin) define base privilege levels with hierarchical precedence; (2) Role registrations map actions to roles, with role-to-permission mappings maintained in both the service and database; (3) Middleware guards enforce permissions via Evaluator objects that check user permissions against required actions/scopes; (4) Dashboard and folder permissions inherit from parent folders through ancestor scope resolution; (5) The AccessControl service coordinates permission checks using an in-memory role cache and database-backed permission store; (6) PermissionsService handles resource-level permission assignment and management for users, teams, and built-in roles.\"\n}\n",
